Exit Site
If you are in danger, call 911. If you need to exit this website quickly, click on the ESCAPE button. This button will immediately open a browser window for weather.com and replace your current window with google.com.

## The .gov means it's official. 
Local, state, and federal government websites often end in .gov. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania government websites and email systems use "pennsylvania.gov" or "pa.gov" at the end of the address. Before sharing sensitive or personal information, make sure you're on an official state website.

  5. Laboratory Improvement


# ​​​​Laboratory Improvement
## What’s New & Important
  * **Beginning in 2026, the Pennsylvania Clinical Laboratory Permit annual licensure invoices will be sent electronically**.
  * **Interpretive Guidance for Laboratory Directors Responsibilities and Duties**.
  * **Transition to Paperless – Email Notifications**.
  * Frequently Asked Questions on Interpretive Guidance on Directors On -site visits and Email Notifications
  * Updated Understanding Clinical Laboratory Regulations in Pennsylvania
  * Application Process and Demo Changes Instructions
  * Pennsylvania Clinical Laboratory Permit Application for In – State laboratories
  * Updated Change of status form
  * Pennsylvania Clinical Laboratory Directors Attestation Statement


The Division of Laboratory Improvement implements state and federal laboratory licensure laws, which apply to Pennsylvania's over 9,000 clinical laboratories. On-site inspections, proficiency assessment and personnel training are utilized to ensure laboratories generate accurate and reliable results. The division also collects data regarding the testing of sexual assault evidence as required by the Pennsylvania Sexual Assault Testing and Evidence Collection Act.
## The Pennsylvania Clinical Laboratory Act and the Clinical Laboratory Improvement Amendments of 1988
### Documents

### Clinical Laboratory Improvement Amendments

### The Pennsylvania Sexual Assault Testing and Evidence Collection Act
On July 10, 2015, Governor Wolf signed Act 27 which amended the Sexual Assault Testing and Evidence Collection Act (Act), 35 P.S. §§ 10172.1-10172.5. Under the Act, local law enforcement agencies have responsibility to take possession of the sexual assault evidence collected by health care facilities for sexual assaults reported to have occurred in the agency's jurisdiction and, upon receipt of consent from the victim, to submit the evidence awaiting testing to a laboratory approved by the Department of Health (Department) for testing or analysis. _See_ 35 P.S. § 10172.3(c)(1) and (3) (relating to sexual assault evidence collection program).
The Act requires local law enforcement agencies and testing laboratories to submit certain reports to the Department, in a form and manner prescribed by the Department, regarding the status of laboratory testing of sexual assault evidence. The Act requires initial reporting by local law enforcement agencies of sexual assault evidence awaiting testing and by laboratories of sexual assault evidence submitted for testing but not yet analyzed by the laboratory, collectively referred to as "Inventory." _See_ 35 P.S. § 10172.3(d). _See_ 35 P.S. § 10172.3(e).
On September 6, 2016, the Department and the Pennsylvania State Police (PSP) signed a Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) to improve the way both agencies will work together in establishing the laboratory standards and data collection procedures regarding sexual assault testing and evidence collection. The PSP will now assist in establishing the forensic laboratory guidelines and gathering the annual backlogged data reports mandated by Act 27 from approved laboratories and Law Enforcement Agencies. Effective Jan 1, 2017, the PSP Bureau of Forensic Services (BFS) will be collecting and collating the data from Pennsylvania Law Enforcement agencies and testing laboratories through an online electronic survey system (SurveyMonkey). **The Pennsylvania Department of Health developed reporting forms previously used will no longer be required.**
All reporting agencies should register with the new Act 27 reporting process by sending an email to the following email address: RA-SPFORENSICSERVICE@pa.gov
Sending an email message to the above email address will ensure that a law enforcement agency or approved testing laboratory is registered on the distribution list for Act 27 reporting information and updates. This will also ensure that the listing of currently active Law Enforcement Agencies is up to date. Additionally, each agency registered on the distribution list will be provided with a link to the online survey (SurveyMonkey) for collection of the data for the annual Act 27 report(s).
#### Applicable Dates for Preparation and Submission of Annual Reports
Reports of Backlogged Evidence must be submitted annually by January 31. If no backlogged evidence exists, local law enforcement agencies and laboratories are still required to complete annual report with that information by January 31. With the 2016 Annual report and going forward, the all reporting agencies must contact the Pennsylvania State Police Bureau of Forensic Services via email at: RA-SPFORENSICSERVICE@pa.gov
Email contact to the above address will ensure the reporting agency is added to the distribution list and will be provided with a link to the online electronic survey (SurveyMonkey) where the reporting will be collected.
**DO NOT SUBMIT REPORTS DIRECTLY TO THE DEPARTMENT OF HEALTH AS DONE IN 2015/2016!**
#### Additional Information related to Act 27
  * [Act 27 Frequently Asked Questions(opens in a new tab)](https://www.pa.gov/content/dam/copapwp-pagov/en/health/documents/topics/documents/laboratories/Act%2027%20FAQs.pdf)

## _Appendix A 115_
Page 3 of 115
* * *
Overview The Sexual Assault Testing and Evidence Collection Act (SATEC) created a sexual assault evidence collection program to promote the health and safety of victims of sexual assault and to facilitate the prosecution of persons accused of sexual assault.
* * *
Under the SATEC, the Pennsylvania Department of Health (Department)—in consultation with the Pennsylvania State Police (PSP), Respect Together, and others—has developed minimum standards requirements for sexual assault evidence collection kits; established training programs on the correct use of these kits; and approved laboratories to receive, test, and analyze sexual assault evidence (35 P.S. § 10172.3(a)). The SATEC further requires the PSP to ensure the analysis and testing of sexual assault evidence (35 P.S. § 10172.3(b)).
* * *
The SATEC created requirements for the submission and testing of sexual assault evidence (35 P.S. § 10172.3(c), (c.1)): • Health care facilities must notify the local law enforcement agency or the Pennsylvania State Police within 12 hours of collecting sexual assault evidence. • The local law enforcement agency or the Pennsylvania State Police must take possession of the evidence from the health care facility within 72 hours. If they don’t, the health care facility must notify the Department using a designated phone number. • Within 15 days of receiving written notice of consent from the victim or victim advocate, the local law enforcement agency must submit the evidence to an approved laboratory for testing or analysis. • Testing of evidence must be completed within six months of it being submitted to an approved laboratory.
* * *
The SATEC established civil immunity for health care professionals and institutions that provide information to law enforcement pursuant to the Act (35 P.S. § 10172.4). The SATEC also created specific rights for sexual assault victims and their guardians or close relatives (35 P.S. § 10172.5).
* * *
Under the SATEC, PSP must submit an annual report to the Department with the volume of sexual assault kits for which testing is completed, the volume of backlogged sexual assault evidence awaiting testing, the average turnaround time to complete testing and the reasons for any delays, and (every two years) a review of current practices in sexual assault evidence collection (35 P.S. § 10172.6). This year’s report submitted by PSP to the Department is provided in Appendix A.
* * *
Each year, every laboratory and local law enforcement agency must report backlogged sexual assault evidence data to the Department. The Department then publishes a report summarizing this data. This annual report is intended to provide a comprehensive overview of the number of backlogged sexual assault kits awaiting testing in the Commonwealth and to ensure that those kits are tested in a timely fashion.
* * *
Page 4 of 115
* * *
Methods As mandated by the SATEC, local law enforcement agencies are required to report the number of backlogged sexual assault kits in their inventory awaiting testing (35 P.S. § 10172.3(e)(1)).
* * *
Backlogged evidence is “sexual assault evidence that is awaiting testing for 12 months or more.” 35 P.S. § 10172.2. Evidence is awaiting testing if it meets all the following conditions (35 P.S. § 10172.2): • Has been collected and is in the possession of a local law enforcement agency; • Has not received DNA or other appropriate forensic analyses; • Is related to a criminal case or investigation where final disposition has not been reached; and • Should undergo DNA or other appropriate forensic analysis as determined by a local law enforcement agency.
* * *
For purposes of this report, local law enforcement agencies include the police department of a city, borough, incorporated town or township; a regional police department; the Pennsylvania State Police; and campus police. 35 P.S. § 10172.2.
* * *
Law enforcement agencies were notified by mail and email of the annual reporting requirements of Act 29 of 2019 as well as the ongoing requirement to report backlogged sexual assault evidence. Questions in this year’s survey were the same as last year. Law enforcement agencies were asked to provide the number of sexual assault kits in the following categories: • Backlogged sexual assault evidence kits awaiting testing; • Kits for which no consent to test was obtained; • Kits from anonymous reporters; and • Kits for which the jurisdiction of the assault was unknown.
* * *
Page 5 of 115
* * *
Findings A total of 1,140 law enforcement agencies reported results. This is a slight decrease from last year, which may be attributed to multiple merged or disbanded law enforcement agencies.
* * *
The agencies reported 317 backlogged sexual assault kits awaiting testing (i.e., kits that have been awaiting testing for 12 months or more) at the end of 2023. This is a 79% increase over the number of backlogged kits compared to the end of 2022 (177 kits), and a 74% decrease in the number of backlogged kits compared to the end of 2016 (1,214 kits).
* * *
Police departments are also in possession of 1,066 kits where the victim has not consented to having the kit tested, 427 kits where the victim is anonymous, and 166 kits where the assault occurred in an unknown jurisdiction. It should be noted that in many cases with anonymous victims, the jurisdiction is also unknown.
* * *

--- EMBEDDED FILE CONTENT: https://www.pa.gov/content/dam/copapwp-pagov/en/health/documents/topics/documents/laboratories/Application%20Process%20and%20Demo%20Changes%20Instructions.pdf ---

Instructions for the Application Process (REV 10/2025) Page 1 of 6 Bureau of Laboratories | 110 Pickering Way, Exton PA 19341 | Phone (610) 280 -3464 | Fax (610) 450 -1932 | www.health.pa.gov/labs Instructions for the Application Process and Demographic Changes A PPLICATION PROCESS FOR ALL NEW PENNSYLVANIA LABORATORIES 1. A laboratory must have both a federal Clinical Laboratory Improvement Amendments (CLIA) certificate and a Pennsylvania clinical laboratory permit (see exceptions below). 2. Complete and return a Clinical Laboratory Application together with a $100 initial filing fee. The federal CLIA application (CMS-116 form) must be included with the state application. The Centers for Medicare & Medicaid Services (CMS) will bill the laboratory separately. 3. A copy of the director’s medical license, any board certifications (if applicable), and any Continuing E ducational Units (CEUs) (if applicable) must be included with the application. For the Department to qual ify a director as a moderate or high complexity director under CLIA, additional documents may be r equired. 4. Annual licensure fees will be billed each year and must be paid by the invoice due date for a permit to be r enewed (see fees below). A DDITIONAL REQUIREMENTS FOR LABORATORIES APPLYING FOR A CLIA CERTIFICATE OF WAIVER (COW) 1. O nce the above listed information is received by the Department and the CMS/CLIA fee has been paid, a laboratory permit will be issued. 2. Any CLIA-waived laboratory may be subject to an on-site inspection as part of a CLIA COW laboratory project. A DDITIONAL REQUIREMENTS FOR LABORATORIES APPLYING FOR A CLIA CERTIFICATE OF PROVIDER PERFORMED MICROSCOPIC PROCEDURES (PPMP) 1. O nce the above listed information is received by the Department and the CMS/CLIA fee has been paid, a laboratory permit will be issued. 2. The laboratory must enroll in a proficiency testing program or implement a policy for performing peer review at least twice per year for PPMP procedures. 3. Any CLIA-PPMP laboratory may be subject to an on-site inspection as part of a CLIA Certificate o f P PMP laboratory project. A DDITIONAL REQUIREMENTS FOR LABORATORIES APPLYING FOR A CLIA CERTIFICATE OF COMPLIANCE 1. O nce the above listed information is received by the Department, a letter of acknowledgement will be s ent to the laboratory indicating the need for an on-site survey. The laboratory may be given pr ovisional approval to begin testing. 2. The laboratory must enroll in a proficiency testing program for CLIA regulated analytes. The laboratory must have a method to verify non-regulated analytes at least twice a year. 3. After approximately 90 days, a Lab Examiner will contact the laboratory to schedule an on-sit e i nspection. 4. Once the laboratory is found to be in complete compliance with state and federal CLIA requirements, a clinical laboratory permit will be issued.
* * *
Instructions for the Application Process (REV 10/2025) Page 2 of 6
* * *
Bureau of Laboratories | 110 Pickering Way, Exton PA 19341 | Phone (610) 280-3464 | Fax (610) 450-1932 | www.health.pa.gov/labs
* * *
ADDITIONAL REQUIREMENTS FOR LABORATORIES APPLYING FOR A CLIA CERTIFICATE OF ACCREDITATION
* * *
1. Once the above listed information is received by the Department, a letter of acknowledgement will be sent to the laboratory indicating the need for an on-site survey. No testing may be performed until the laboratory has been notified by the Department that licensure is in effect. 2. The laboratory must enroll in a proficiency testing program for CLIA regulated analytes. The laboratory must have a method to verify non-regulated analytes at least twice a year. 3. The laboratory must provide a letter of acknowledgement from the accrediting organization to which it has applied. 4. A Lab Examiner will contact the laboratory to schedule an on-site inspection. 5. Once the laboratory is found to be in complete compliance with state and federal CLIA requirements, a clinical laboratory permit will be issued.
* * *
ADDITIONAL REQUIREMENTS FOR LABORATORIES PERFORMING TOXICOLOGY, BLOOD LEAD, OR ERYTHROCYTE PROTOPORPHYRIN TESTING
* * *
1. Laboratories requesting licensure to perform quantitative testing for drugs in blood and/or serum or urine, alcohol, blood lead or erythrocyte protoporphyrin must be approved by the Department’s Division of Chemistry and Toxicology. 2. Laboratories performing this testing must be enrolled in the Pennsylvania Toxicology Proficiency Testing Program. 3. Once the above listed information is received by the Department, an invoice will be sent to the laboratory for all applicable proficiency testing fees. 4. Once the fees have been paid, pre-licensure proficiency testing specimens will be sent to the laboratory. 5. Once proficiency testing samples have been tested and results are found to be acceptable, a letter of acknowledgement will be sent to the laboratory indicating the need for an on-site survey. 6. The above requirements will be followed based on CLIA certificate type.
* * *
EXCEPTIONS FOR OBTAINING A PENNSYLVANIA CLINICAL LABORATORY PERMIT
* * *
A permit is NOT required under the following instances:
* * *
1. Ambulance Services performing glucose testing ONLY 2. Plasma centers 3. Home Health and Home Hospice Services performing testing for Home Use ONLY
* * *
OUT OF STATE PERFORMING TESTNG ON PENNSYLVANIA RESIDENTS
* * *
Laboratories outside of the Commonwealth performing testing on specimens originating from the Commonwealth must have a valid Pennsylvania Clinical Laboratory Permit. Follow the instructions above for submitting the appropriate application.
* * *
Instructions for the Application Process (REV 10/2025) Page 3 of 6
* * *
Bureau of Laboratories | 110 Pickering Way, Exton PA 19341 | Phone (610) 280-3464 | Fax (610) 450-1932 | www.health.pa.gov/labs
* * *
OVERSIGHT OF MORE THAN TWO (2) CLINICAL LABORATORIES IN PA
* * *
The Department continues to exercise enforcement discretion of 28 Pa. Code § 5.22 (f) to allow laboratory directors to oversee more than two clinical laboratories with proper documentation.
* * *
1. The laboratory director must complete and submit an attestation form indicating the laboratory director understands and will complete their duties for each laboratory they plan to oversee. 2. A copy of the director’s medical license, any board certifications (if applicable), and any CEUs (if applicable) must be included with the application. For the Department to qualify a director as a moderate or high complexity director under CLIA, additional documents may be required.
* * *
ANNUAL FEES
* * *
LICENSURE FEES: Clinical Chemistry including Urinalysis.................................... $100 Microbiology including Syphilis & Non-Syphilis Serology …. …… $100 Hematology including Immunohematology ………………………… $100 Tissue Pathology including Exfoliative Cytology ……………….. $100 Radioisotope Technics ……………………………………………… $100
* * *
PROFICIENCY TESTING FEES: (See Division of Chemistry and Toxicology – Toxicology Proficiency Testing Program Fees)
* * *
Payment Options:
* * *
Payment for renewals may be made on-line with a credit card at www.PALabsBillPayment.health.pa.gov or Payment may be submitted by check or money order, made payable to the Pennsylvania Department of Health. Failure to pay on or before August 15 will result in the revocation of your Pennsylvania laboratory permit pursuant to Section 2156 (b) of the Clinical Laboratory Act, 35 P.S. § 2151§ 2165. Once a laboratory receives a revocation notice, the laboratory must reapply for their license. In addition, the outstanding balance and application fees must be paid.
* * *
MULTISITE CERTIFICATION/LICENSURE
* * *
CLIA allows for multiple laboratory locations to be covered by a single CLIA certificate. In order to apply for the CLIA multiple site certificate, the laboratories must meet one or more of the following regulatory exceptions:
* * *
• A laboratory that has temporary testing sites • A not-for-profit or federal, state, or local government laboratory engaged in limited public health testing (no more than a combination of 15 waived or moderate complexity tests) being performed at multiple testing sites • A hospital with multiple testing sites located at contiguous buildings on the same campus within the same physical location or street address and under common direction
* * *
There is no provision in the Clinical Laboratory Act for multisite licensure. Each testing site must apply for and maintain a separate clinical laboratory permit.
* * *
Instructions for the Application Process (REV 10/2025) Page 4 of 6
* * *
Bureau of Laboratories | 110 Pickering Way, Exton PA 19341 | Phone (610) 280-3464 | Fax (610) 450-1932 | www.health.pa.gov/labs
* * *
LABORATORY PERMIT TO OPERATE SCREENING SITES
* * *
Screening sites are locations where certain tests are performed on a temporary basis. The following situations require a Pennsylvania clinical laboratory permit to operate screening sites:
* * *
• The collection and testing of specimens at temporary sites. An organization may visit the same site multiple times. However, testing supplies may not be stored at the site between visits.
* * *
An application to operate screening sites must be submitted to the Bureau along with supporting documentation. A screening site permit must be issued before patient testing may be performed.
* * *
Note: On-site testing is limited to CLIA-waived instruments/test kits only.
* * *
LABORATORY PERMIT TO OPERATE A MOBILE LAB
* * *
A mobile laboratory is a movable, self-contained, operational laboratory with its own personnel, equipment, and records. Testing performed inside a vehicle which travels between temporary testing sites requires a laboratory permit to operate a mobile laboratory, not a permit to operate screening sites. A CLIA certificate is also required for the mobile laboratory. A vehicle which is only used to transport testing supplies/staff between temporary testing sites is not considered a mobile laboratory if no testing takes place inside the vehicle.
* * *
An application to operate a mobile laboratory must be submitted to the Bureau along with supporting documentation. A mobile lab permit must be issued before patient testing may be performed.
* * *
Note: If an organization performs testing at some temporary sites using a mobile laboratory and testing at other temporary sites without the mobile laboratory, it must obtain both a Pennsylvania clinical laboratory permit to operate a mobile laboratory and a permit to operate screening sites.
* * *
CLINICAL LABORATORY PERMIT CHANGES
* * *
The laboratory must notify the Bureau immediately of a change in director or location and within 30 days of a change in owner, laboratory name or test menu. To facilitate this process, the laboratory must complete and submit a Change of Status form to the Bureau of Laboratories. Once received, changes will be made to both the State permit and CLIA certificate, if applicable.
* * *
REQUIREMENTS FOR SUBMISSION OF A CMS 116 FORM
* * *
ALL LABORATORIES • Change of ownership • Certificate type change to PPMP, Compliance or Accreditation • Adding a multiple site exception • Personnel – Director (PPM, Certificate of Compliance)
* * *
Instructions for the Application Process (REV 10/2025) Page 5 of 6
* * *
Bureau of Laboratories | 110 Pickering Way, Exton PA 19341 | Phone (610) 280-3464 | Fax (610) 450-1932 | www.health.pa.gov/labs
* * *
REQUIREMENTS FOR SUBMISSION OF A CHANGE OF STATUS FORM
* * *
ALL LABORATORIES
* * *
• Change of director – Must also submit a copy of the director’s medical license, and board certifications, if applicable • Change of address (physical/mailing/billing) • Change of laboratory name • Change of ownership – You must also submit an updated CMS 116 Form • Change of federal tax ID number • Change of State permit type (ex. Physician’s Office Lab to Independent Lab) • Lab is closing or discontinuing all clinical testing • Change of CLIA certificate type (ex. Waiver to Compliance) – If changing to PPMP, Compliance or Accreditation, you must also submit an updated CMS-116 Form
* * *
PHYSICIAN’S OFFICE LABORATORIES
* * *
• Change in test menu, such as adding and/or deleting tests – When adding a test, include the FDA 510(K) number • Changing from a waived method to a non-waived kit/method for the same analyte (NOT changing from one waived kit/method to another) • Changing from a non-waived method to a waived kit/method for the same analyte
* * *
ALL OTHER LABORATORIES
* * *
• Change in test menu, such as adding a category of testing (ex. Hematology, Clinical Chemistry) when the laboratory is not currently licensed to perform testing in that category or deleting a category of testing when the laboratory is authorized to perform unlimited testing in that category
* * *
• Change in any Toxicology testing, including adding and/or deleting tests and changing from one test method to another for the same analyte
* * *
Do not submit copies of procedures, validation studies, training documentation, etc. unless requested. Please keep these documents to be reviewed at the time of your next on-site inspection.
* * *
The Change of Status Form must be signed by the director for a director change to be valid. For all other changes, the form may be signed by the director and/or owner of the laboratory.
* * *
PLEASE NOTE: If your changes result in a change to your permit, you will receive a confirmation letter from the Department indicating the changes that were made. Please keep this letter with your records.
* * *
If your changes do not result in a change to your permit, your form will be filed. You will not receive a confirmation letter from the Department.
* * *
The Pennsylvania’s Clinical Laboratory Act requires that a clinical laboratory be overseen by a qualified laboratory director who provides direct and personal supervision of the laboratory’s operation. The Department requires each laboratory director to complete and sign a director’s attestation form. This is for the Director to attest to their willingness to assume all directorship responsibilities for the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania purposes, and to understand that they are responsible for the accuracy and reliability of all testing performed to ensure that the laboratory meets and will continue to meet the requirements of the Clinical Laboratory Act (CLA), 35 P.S § 2151§ 2165, and its regulations, 28 Pa Code § 5.1§ 5. 104.
* * *
Instructions for the Application Process (REV 10/2025) Page 6 of 6
* * *
Bureau of Laboratories | 110 Pickering Way, Exton PA 19341 | Phone (610) 280-3464 | Fax (610) 450-1932 | www.health.pa.gov/labs
* * *
## Pa. Code § 5.22(g) requires that a director be present for a reasonable period of each working day in each
laboratory for which they are a director. The Department interprets the term “present” to include a
* * *
remote/virtual (i.e., telephonic, email, video conferencing) presence, as well as a physical on-site presence.
* * *
Directors of laboratories performing only waived testing are required to be continuously available virtually to the laboratory during all times when testing is performed to provide telephone or electronic consultation as needed. For laboratories performing moderate/high complexity testing, the Department requires the director to be on site once every 6 months, with at least 4 months between the minimum two on-site visits. The director’s on-site visits may not be delegated. The on-site visits combined with the daily remote presence enables the director to participate and actively oversee the planning, organization, direction and review of all laboratory operations to the extent necessary to ensure compliance with the regulations, including ensuring the proper storage and quality of reagents, supplies. The director is required to provide documentation of the on-site visits, including evidence of performing activities that are part of the laboratory director’s responsibilities, upon request by the Department of Health.
* * *
The Clinical Laboratory Act regulations define a supervisor as “[a] properly qualified individual, who, under the direction of an authorized director, may supervise the general activities of a clinical laboratory, or a properly qualified individual who under the direction of an authorized director, may supervise the technical work in a laboratory category.” If the Director will not be on-site during all hours of testing, then the Director must employ a qualified general supervisor who will be on the premises during all normal scheduled working hours in which tests are being performed.
* * *
SUPERVISOR QUALIFICATIONS AND INTERPRETATION OF ACCEPTABLE EXPERIENCE FOR LABORATORIES THAT PERFORM NON-WAIVED TESTING.
* * *
## _28 Pa Code § 5.23. requires 2 years’ experience acceptable to the Department for a doctoral degree, 4 years’_
experience for a M.A or M.S. degree or 6 years’ experience for a B.S. or B.A. with major in biological, physical,
* * *
or chemical sciences. The Department interprets the term “acceptable experience” for laboratories performing non-waived tests to include: • • Performing non-waived testing OR • • Other experience as determined and documented by the laboratory director to be appropriate.
* * *
PLEASE NOTE: THE EDUCATIONAL QUALIFICATION REQUIREMENTS MUST BE MET.
* * *

## _Appendix A 113_
UNTESTED SEXUAL ASSAULT KITS AND BACKLOGGED EVIDENCE PENNSYLVANIA DEPARTMENT OF HEALTH 3
* * *
Overview The Sexual Assault Testing and Evidence Collection Act (SATEC) was amended by Act 164 of 2018. Act 164 provides a sexual assault evidence collection program that grants responsibilities to the Pennsylvania Department of Health (Department) and the Pennsylvania State Police (PSP) to establish civil immunity and provide for rights of sexual assault victims, while giving PSP the task to complete and submit a biannual report to the Department of Health (SATEC Act 164 of 2018). Act 164 was signed by Governor Wolf on October 24, 2018, and went into effect on December 23, 2018 (SATEC Act 164 of 2018). Act 164 was further amended in 2019 (Act 29) and was signed by Governor Wolf on June 28, 2019.
* * *
Act 164 made several changes to the existing version of the SATEC. First, a new statutory provision, 35 P.S. §§ 10172.6, was created that mandated biannual reporting requirements on PSP. The newly created provision within the SATEC requires PSP to make an initial report to the Department by December 31, 2018, and every six months thereafter. The PSP report must include the volume of sexual assault kits for which testing is completed, the average turnaround time to complete testing and the reasons for any delays. The report submitted from PSP to the Department is Appendix A.
* * *
Additional changes to the SATEC (Act 29 of 2019) include: • Biannual reporting was changed to annual reporting; • Mandates the reporting of a review of current practices, including interagency collaboration with law enforcement agencies and rape crisis centers, in rape kit evidence collection every two years; • Establishment of a designated telephone number for health care facilities to call when law enforcement fails to take possession of the kit within 72 hours; • Health care facilities must notify law enforcement within 12 hours of collecting sexual assault evidence; and • Testing of evidence must be completed within six months of it being submitted to an approved lab.
* * *
Every year by April 30, the Department is required to publish a report summarizing the information submitted by local law enforcement agencies to its website. This annual report is intended to provide a comprehensive overview of the number of untested sexual assault kits in the commonwealth and to ensure that those kits are tested in a timely fashion.
* * *
UNTESTED SEXUAL ASSAULT KITS AND BACKLOGGED EVIDENCE PENNSYLVANIA DEPARTMENT OF HEALTH 4
* * *
Methods As mandated by the SATEC, law enforcement agencies were required to report the number of sexual assault kits in their possession with backlogged evidence awaiting testing as of December 31, 2022. The SATEC defines backlogged evidence as “sexual assault evidence that is awaiting testing for 12 months or more” (35 P.S. 10172.2). Evidence is awaiting testing if it meets all the following conditions: • Has been collected and is in the possession of a local law enforcement agency; • Has not received DNA or other appropriate forensic analyses; • Is related to a criminal case or investigation where final disposition has not been reached; and • Should undergo DNA or other appropriate forensic analysis as determined by a local law enforcement agency.
* * *
Law enforcement agencies were notified by mail and email of th e annual reporting requirements of Act 29 of 2019, as well as the ongoing requirement to report backlogged sexual assault evidence. Questions in this year’s survey were the same as last year. Law enforcement agencies were asked to provide the number of sexual assault kits in the following categories: • Backlogged kits awaiting testing; • Kits for which no consent to test was obtained; • Kits from anonymous reporters; and • Kits for which the jurisdiction of the assault was unknown.
* * *
UNTESTED SEXUAL ASSAULT KITS AND BACKLOGGED EVIDENCE PENNSYLVANIA DEPARTMENT OF HEALTH 5
* * *
Findings A total of 1,172 law enforcement agencies, reported results. This is the highest number of reporting agencies since the inception of the mandatory reporting in accordance with the statute. The agencies, including campus police and approved laboratories, reported 177 backlogged sexual assault kits awaiting testing at the end of 2022. This is a 5% decrease over the number of backlogged kits compared to the end of 2021, and an 85% decrease compared to the end of 2016. Police departments are also in possession of 980 kits where the victim has not consented to having the kit tested, 437 kits where the victim is anonymous and 127 kits where the assault occurred in an unknown jurisdiction. It should be noted that in many cases with anonymous victims, the jurisdiction is also unknown.
* * *
## _Table 1 includes an overview of the number of sexual assault kits awaiting testing as of February_
2023. It also provides an overview of the number of kits for which the victim did not consent to
* * *
testing, kits with anonymous victims and kits for which the assault occurred in an unknown jurisdiction.

* * *
not consent to testing, the number of kits from an anonymous victim (Jane Doe kit) and the number of kits where the assault occurred in an unknown jurisdiction.

## _Appendix A_
PENNSYLVANIA STATE POLICE
* * *
DEPARTMENT CORRESPONDENCE
* * *
DATE: February 23, 2023 SUBJECT: Pennsylvania Sexual Assault Testing and Evidence Collection Act Survey for Mandatory Reporting for 2022 TO: Kristen Rodack Director, Office of Policy Pennsylvania Department of Health FROM: Peggy J. Moody-Kosman Assistant Director, Scientific Services Division, Bureau of Forensic Services, Pennsylvania State Police
* * *
ENCLOSURES: (1) Letter to Law Enforcement Agencies dated November 16, 2022 (2) Email Alert sent to Law Enforcement Agencies on December 13, 2022 (3) Copy of Surveys sent to Law Enforcement Agencies and PA State Police via SurveyMonkey on January 3, 2023 (4) Email sent to Pennsylvania Chiefs of Police Association on January 6, 2023 (5) Reminder Letter to Law Enforcement Agencies dated January 19, 2023 (6) Excel Spreadsheet of Survey Results for the Mandatory Reporting of Sexual Assault Evidence 1. Actions taken for the collection of data regarding the number of sexual assault evidence awaiting testing as of December 31, 2022, included the following. October 2022 • List of Law Enforcement Agencies (LEA) including campus police and approved laboratories with active ORI numbers obtained from the CLEAN Administrative Section, Pennsylvania State Police (PSP). November 2022 • Letter dated November 16, 2022, mailed to LEA with dates of Email Alert (12/13/22) and Survey (1/3/23). See Enclosure (1). • eBulletin sent to PSP personnel instructing PSP Bureaus and Stations to submit point of contact information for PSP reporting.
* * *
UNTESTED SEXUAL ASSAULT KITS AND BACKLOGGED EVIDENCE PENNSYLVANIA DEPARTMENT OF HEALTH 115
* * *
December 2022 • Email Alert sent December 13, 2022 to LEA contacts obtained from CLEAN and to LEA contacts from last year’s survey. Alert stated date of survey and reporting requirement. See Enclosure (2). January 2023 • SurveyMonkey launched January 3, 2023. Two surveys distributed, one to PSP and one to all local LEA. See Enclosure (3) for copy of surveys. • Reminder email sent to those not responding within two weeks after receiving initial survey. • Email sent to Pennsylvania Chiefs of Police Association on January 6, 2023. See Enclosure (4). • Reminder letter dated January 19, 2023 mailed to LEA not yet reporting. See Enclosure (5). February 2023 • Emails sent between February 3 – 6, 2023 to district attorneys asking their assistance in notifying non-reporting agencies. • Reminder emails sent to non-reporting agencies. • Survey closed February 21, 2023. No additional responses accepted.
* * *
2. Efforts were made to update the list of active LEA for this year’s survey. The high number of small and part time LEA within Pennsylvania lead to chronic changes in status, personnel and location. Between December and February, PSP Bureau of Forensic Services provided responses to over 500 email and phone call inquiries from LEA seeking guidance regarding the mandatory reporting. Some respondents provided information regarding LEA currently disbanded, merged with other agencies or otherwise inactive. One question in the survey requested a list of municipalities serviced by the reporting agency. Inactive LEA were removed from the list if their municipality was serviced by another law enforcement agency.
* * *
3. Additional four-year colleges and universities within Pennsylvania not on the list with active ORI numbers were again targeted this year to participate in the survey. This was to ensure all campus police/security had the opportunity to report out any sexual assault evidence that may be in their custody. Although campus police are mandated to report out yearly, it is difficult to determine which colleges and universities have police or security departments.
* * *
4. Questions in this year’s survey were the same as last year. Law enforcement agencies were asked to provide the number of sexual assault kits in the following categories: backlogged kits awaiting testing, kits where no consent to test was obtained, kits from anonymous reporters, and kits where the jurisdiction of the assault was unknown.
* * *
5. The results of the survey for the mandatory reporting of sexual assault evidence are found in Enclosure (6). The Excel spreadsheet contains two tabs: 1) reporting agencies listed by county and 2) non-reporting agencies. The number of kits reported by each agency are listed in columns G through K. The list of non-reporting agencies was determined using the agencies with currently active ORI numbers as per CLEAN where no other information was
* * *
UNTESTED SEXUAL ASSAULT KITS AND BACKLOGGED EVIDENCE PENNSYLVANIA DEPARTMENT OF HEALTH 116
* * *
provided to indicate the agency was disbanded, merged with another agency or otherwise inactive as well as four-year colleges and universities within Pennsylvania.
* * *
6. In summary, a total of 1,172 law enforcement agencies, reported results. This is the highest number of reporting agencies since the inception of the mandatory reporting in accordance with the statute. The agencies, including campus police and approved laboratories, reported 177 backlogged sexual assault kits awaiting testing at the end of 2022. This is a 5% decrease over the number of backlogged kits compared to the end of 2021, and an 85% decrease compared to the end of 2016. Police departments are also in possession of 980 kits where the victim has not consented to having the kit tested, 437 kits where the victim is anonymous and 127 kits where the assault occurred in an unknown jurisdiction. It should be noted that in many cases with anonymous victims, the jurisdiction is also unknown.
* * *
7. The Non-Reporting Agencies listed in Enclosure (6) include the mailing address that the PSP contacted in an unsuccessful attempt to obtain data for this reporting period. As the Pennsylvania Department of Health (DOH) is ultimately responsible for obtaining backlogged evidence data from non-reporting sources, this information is provided to DOH for its information and review.
* * *
8. Under the most recent amendment to the Sexual Assault Testing and Evidence Collection statute, the PA State Police is to annually report the volume of sexual assault kits for which testing is completed, the average turnaround time to complete testing, and the reasons for any delays. The data from the three approved forensic laboratories within Pennsylvania is listed in the table below.
* * *
The average turnaround time to complete testing is calculated from the time the evidence is first submitted to the lab until the reports are completed.
* * *
LABORATORY Cases Completed Average Turnaround Time Allegheny County Office of the Medical Examiner Forensic Laboratory (ACOME) 129 6.4 months* Pennsylvania State Police Bureau of Forensic Services 963 103 days Philadelphia Police Department Office of Forensic Sciences 462 115 days TOTAL 1,554
* * *
* The average turnround time of receipt of the item to issuance of a report was 6.4 months. The turnaround time was impacted due to three scientists of the Forensic Biology section focusing on the completion of their training in 2022 (two qualifying for serology analysis and one for DNA analysis). In addition, ACOME had several members of the unit accept employment with other organizations in 2022. Those individuals included one Forensic Biology Scientist (fully trained in Serology Analysis), the Forensic Biology Manager (a fully trained DNA analyst) and the DNA Technical Leader (a fully trained DNA analyst) all of whom previously contributed to case production.
* * *
